Even getting by shopping at malls and super markets used to feel like a huge achievement. Things changed, but Gainesville will always remain close to my heart. Recently, I was called to interpret for a case at Hall County Court House in Gainesville. It felt great to go back to the city where I started my American journey. And this time, not to drive by and show our family and friends where I started life in the US, but to actually work at one of their biggest legal operations! Life changes, but memories remain constant and help you make new ones. And yes, I shared this story with every possible person I met in the courthouse that day\uD83D\uDE00!!\" - Sumana Goswami Sumana Goswami is a professional interpreter, and a model. So being Indian was always my family's thing, it was a very insular identity and the language we speak, Malayalam, was like our language, since I didn't know people who spoke it. I didn't know many Indian people, or at least for those five years I was in Japan and even once I got here. It was like being Indian for me as a big statement. Especially for me, it was always being South Indian or being Malayali or being Indian Muslim. I feel like there's a lot of little identities within being Indian that have so much value to me. So being Indian has just been a lot of connection to my immediate family, especially because a lot of us don't see much extended family and everything, so you have to rely on your immediate family or like your friends at school, who might be different types of ‘Indian.’ My experience has really been shaped by the people I have in my life. So it's been a combination of having friends who are from different parts of India. And then my family members were the only people I knew with like the exact identity, religious, cultural identity that I had. In my freshman year world literature class we read a book that was set in Kerala. That was a really cool experience for me and it kind of inspired me to take Malayalam at UT. Reading that book and having Malayalam discussed in class was just crazy…. I just really had a revelation that day because I was so weirded out by people talking about things that had always been my family's thing, but in a cool way! We will also be supporting the outgoing princess Olivia Samaniego raise awareness during her red dress jingle dress special in honor of MMIWG2S. MMIW Texas will collect single earrings for our “in-progress” earring exhibit (which is modeled after the Sing Our Rivers Red earring exhibit we hosted last September at Oak Cliff Cultural Center in Dallas, Texas). We are focusing on collecting community members’ personal single earrings. If individual’s have information (name, tribe, where they’re from) on the MMIWG2S (Missing & Murdered Indigenous Women, Girls, and Two-Spirits) you are donating your single earring in honor of, we will take down that information also at our table this Saturday. We are collecting for and creating this earring exhibit to bring awareness and educate about the MMIW crisis in Indian Country. And know the MMIW crisis does hit close to home for us too in our urban area. In the past few months, MMIW Texas has assisted two local American Indian families in locating their teenage daughters who were missing. Thankfully, both teens were found and returned to their families. Earrings can be modern styles like hoops or more traditional Native styles like beaded earrings. American Indians love their earrings and we always have beautiful earrings whether it’s big gold hoops or porcupine quills or dentalium shells. We take pride in wearing them and appreciate the skill and craftsmanship that goes into creating earrings. So when we lose an earring, for some reason we always hold on to that single earring we have left in hopes the other one will show up out of nowhere or be found or just to remember the pair. We look at our MMIW sisters in this same way. Whether they are missing or murdered, we hold on to their memories and keep praying for our sisters to be found and returned home to us - their loved ones and their land. Some individuals have even donated a single earring from a pair they still have both earrings to in the sense that they know the match is not with them and they feel the loss of it and pray for its return. So please consider donating your single earring(s) in honor of one of our Native sisters, whether you know them personally or not, to MMIW Texas to be added to our collection for our future exhibit. Mvto! Wado! Sujatha is a seasoned executive who led highly complex transformational (Technology and Operations) initiatives in various Fortune 500 companies including Cisco, Microsoft, Amazon, and Dell prior to founding Suji Fresh. \n\nHere is how Sujatha described her background and Suji \nFresh in her own words: \n\n\"To understand Suji Fresh and my background better, I need to take us back to my childhood where I grew up in Andhra Pradesh, India. My grandparents, relatives, and family friends were farmers themselves or leased their Orchards to other farmers in the nearby villages. I could barely wait for my summer vacations to start so that I can go see the Mango harvesting in my village.  I used to pick fresh Mangoes off the trees and eat those right there after barely rinsing. Our family gatherings always involved fresh fruit from the Orchards without a concern of what underlying risks lay apparent. There was never a mention of pesticides or chemicals nor have they ever used those in the farms. GMOs (Genetically Modified Organisms) wasn’t even a thing at that time. Water shortages and drought were enough to keep farmers up at night but fortunately those were the days where there was not a concern of “Organic” vs “Conventional” at least in India. All our farms were organic and pesticide-free. These fond memories in lush greens, most pristine atmosphere, and the fresh water from the nearby lake were well preserved and framed in my mind for years to come. \n\nFast forward to 2008. I recall the memories of what happened in 2008 as if it happened yesterday. My daughter had just turned 8. She loved life and loved to dance. She learned and performed an incredibly beautiful Indian dance Art Form called Bharatanatyam from age 5. Life just seemed to have taken a few difficult turns unexpectedly. Our family was experiencing challenging times as I was faced with a traumatic situation of divorce. On top of that, we were faced with a big medical crisis for my daughter. We noticed a patch on my daughter’s hair that seem to grow gradually. The diagnosis came on her 8th birthday. I heard a term that I never heard in my lifetime. Alopecia Areata! What does that even mean? I was told that it is an auto-immune disease that attacks our own body as a foreign object. It attacked her hair. In some cases, the damage could be permanent. We were told it was due to food allergies – and there is NO CURE for it. At least, not with traditional Western Medicine. I learned another new term called “gluten allergy.” Apparently, gluten was attacking her body. We were told to eliminate all the foods that could potentially contain gluten, dairy etc. The integrity of food supply chain has been compromised such that food that was supposed to nourish her was impacting her health. I was heartbroken by this diagnosis and the impact it had on her life and our lives. I was determined to find a cure for her disease even if it meant quitting my job and studying medicine. I poured over in numerous articles and searched for specialist doctors across the world who could cure this condition. We finally got a referral to a doctor near us who practiced an alternative medicine named “Ayurveda.” He prescribed very special oils for her hair, which costed nearly $200-$300 a bottle and not covered by insurance. \nThose 4 years of trials and triumphs changed my life profoundly. When I was faced with life challenges, it transformed me as a human being. I became highly creative with what I had to work with. As they say, necessity is the mother of invention.\nWhat did it take to get here? What was the process for recovery? Food and Meditation! We stopped eating any chemically sprayed food and only bought organic food. It meant that we cut down all our other expenses to be able to afford that. I created many delicious recipes without dairy and gluten and became the go-to-person for my friends dealing with allergies. It taught me the impact of food on our thoughts and how to balance Mind, Body, and Spirit. Now, a team of us manage a channel called “Mind Body Spirit Balance”. Look for our upcoming PODCASTs relating to Mind Body Spirit Balance (@mbsrefresh on FB).  \n\nI have shared my personal journey with all of you in the hope that it becomes a survival guide for others. My kind request for everyone is to think about how we can all contribute to building a better society by bringing ourselves in alignment with Mother Nature and Her ways. When we go against it, not only do we cause a lot of harm to our own health, but also seriously disturb the ecosystem of all other beings that coexist with us. The way we grow food, the way we process dairy products impact our health. This is the main inspiration for creating Suji Fresh. \n\nI think the world is open to a better transition for the well-being of humanity now than ever before. None of us can (truncated)","message":"Ravishing Woman of the Day : SUJATHA PUBBARAJU Sujatha Pubbaraju is the Founder and CEO of Suji Fresh based in the Greater Seattle Area. Sujatha is a seasoned executive who led highly complex transformational (Technology and Operations) initiatives in various Fortune 500 companies including Cisco, Microsoft, Amazon, and Dell prior to founding Suji Fresh. Here is how Sujatha described her background and Suji Fresh in her own words: \"To understand Suji Fresh and my background better, I need to take us back to my childhood where I grew up in Andhra Pradesh, India. My grandparents, relatives, and family friends were farmers themselves or leased their Orchards to other farmers in the nearby villages. I could barely wait for my summer vacations to start so that I can go see the Mango harvesting in my village. I used to pick fresh Mangoes off the trees and eat those right there after barely rinsing. Our family gatherings always involved fresh fruit from the Orchards without a concern of what underlying risks lay apparent. There was never a mention of pesticides or chemicals nor have they ever used those in the farms. GMOs (Genetically Modified Organisms) wasn’t even a thing at that time. Water shortages and drought were enough to keep farmers up at night but fortunately those were the days where there was not a concern of “Organic” vs “Conventional” at least in India. All our farms were organic and pesticide-free. These fond memories in lush greens, most pristine atmosphere, and the fresh water from the nearby lake were well preserved and framed in my mind for years to come. Fast forward to 2008. I recall the memories of what happened in 2008 as if it happened yesterday. My daughter had just turned 8. She loved life and loved to dance. She learned and performed an incredibly beautiful Indian dance Art Form called Bharatanatyam from age 5. Life just seemed to have taken a few difficult turns unexpectedly. Our family was experiencing challenging times as I was faced with a traumatic situation of divorce. On top of that, we were faced with a big medical crisis for my daughter. We noticed a patch on my daughter’s hair that seem to grow gradually. The diagnosis came on her 8th birthday. I heard a term that I never heard in my lifetime. Alopecia Areata! What does that even mean? I was told that it is an auto-immune disease that attacks our own body as a foreign object. It attacked her hair. In some cases, the damage could be permanent. We were told it was due to food allergies – and there is NO CURE for it. At least, not with traditional Western Medicine. I learned another new term called “gluten allergy.” Apparently, gluten was attacking her body. We were told to eliminate all the foods that could potentially contain gluten, dairy etc. The integrity of food supply chain has been compromised such that food that was supposed to nourish her was impacting her health. I was heartbroken by this diagnosis and the impact it had on her life and our lives. I was determined to find a cure for her disease even if it meant quitting my job and studying medicine. I poured over in numerous articles and searched for specialist doctors across the world who could cure this condition. We finally got a referral to a doctor near us who practiced an alternative medicine named “Ayurveda.” He prescribed very special oils for her hair, which costed nearly $200-$300 a bottle and not covered by insurance. Those 4 years of trials and triumphs changed my life profoundly. When I was faced with life challenges, it transformed me as a human being. I became highly creative with what I had to work with. As they say, necessity is the mother of invention. What did it take to get here? What was the process for recovery? Food and Meditation! We stopped eating any chemically sprayed food and only bought organic food. It meant that we cut down all our other expenses to be able to afford that. I created many delicious recipes without dairy and gluten and became the go-to-person for my friends dealing with allergies. It taught me the impact of food on our thoughts and how to balance Mind, Body, and Spirit. Now, a team of us manage a channel called “Mind Body Spirit Balance”. Look for our upcoming PODCASTs relating to Mind Body Spirit Balance (@mbsrefresh on FB). I have shared my personal journey with all of you in the hope that it becomes a survival guide for others. My kind request for everyone is to think about how we can all contribute to building a better society by bringing ourselves in alignment with Mother Nature and Her ways. When we go against it, not only do we cause a lot of harm to our own health, but also seriously disturb the ecosystem of all other beings that coexist with us. The way we grow food, the way we process dairy products impact our health. This is the main inspiration for creating Suji Fresh. I think the world is open to a better transition for the well-being of humanity now than ever before. None of us can do it alone, but विपरीत फल देने वाला ग्रह है । इस लिए ऐसे ग्रहो का गोचर कुण्डली के ३ ६,८ ,१२ वे भाव में होने पर शुभता देता है । इस तरह ८ वे भाव में यह गोचर शुभकारी रहेगा । भले ही ८ वा भाव लम्बे रोग, दुर्घटना और दुख का भाव है , लेकिन गुरु ग्रह शुभकारी ग्रह है । इस लिए यह गोचर पुराने रोग, बीमारी, झगड़े और परेशानी को दूर करेगा, खास कर अगर किसी महिला की वृषभ लग्न है और उनको लम्बे समय से संतान प्राप्ति का इंतजार है तो गुरु का यह गोचर उनको संतान सुख दे सकता है , जिन पुरुषों को नोकरी में तरक्की का इंतजार है या फिर किसी अच्छी नोकरी का इंतजार है उनकी भी यह इच्छा पूरी हो सकती है । कुण्डली के २ रा और ४ था भावो पर गुरु ग्रह की दृष्टि इन विषयों ( धन, परिवारिक सुख, प्रॉपर्टी, वाहन ) की प्राप्ति देगी । \uD83C\uDF39मिथुन लग्न : गुरु ग्रह स्वामी ग्रह है ७ वे और १० वे भावो का, लग्नेश बुध का शत्रु और ७ वे भाव का स्वामी होने के कारण विपरीत फल देने वाला ग्रह है । क्योंकि गुरु ग्रह भोगकारक ग्रह नहीं, सिर्फ विषयो की प्राप्ति का ग्रह है, इस लिए सप्तम भाव से संबंधित विषयों की प्राप्ति ( प्रेमी / प्रेमिका, जीवनसाथी, सरकारी नोकरी, व्यवसाय की शुरुआत ) के लिए समय मदद करेगा , लेकिन भोग के लिए यह समय शुभ नहीं इस लिए जो पहले से व्यवसाय चला रहे हैं उनके लाभ में कमी आएगी इस लिए ७ वे भाव की गुरु ग्रह की शर्त पूरी करें किसी बड़े बुजुर्ग की सलाह को अपने व्यवसायक वृद्धि के लिए शामिल करें । जो गृहस्थ जीवन में हैं नवविवाहित हैं उनके रिश्ते में समस्या आएगी । चाहे प्रोफेशनल हो या पर्सनल हो नए लोगो से जुड़ने पर लाभ और सम्मान की प्राप्ति होगी । \uD83C\uDF39कर्क लग्न : गुरु ग्रह ६ थे और ९ वे भाव का स्वामी ग्रह, लग्नेश चन्द्रमा का मित्र होकर शुभकारी फल देने वाला ग्रह है । ऐसे शुभकारी ग्रह का गोचर कुण्डली के ६ थे भाव में शुभ नहीं होता , क्योंकि कुण्डली का यह भाव रोग स्थान है और गुरु ग्रह घर बड़ो का कारक है , इस लिए घर के बड़ो को कुछ कष्ट रहेगा, सांस और ह्रदय संबंधित रोग होने पर विशेष ध्यान रखें । कुण्डली का ६ ठा भाव का संबंध वास्तु में वायव्ह कोन ( उत्तर - पश्चिम दिशा ) से है इसको रुदन स्थान भी कहा जाता है, यानी नाराज़गी का स्थान इस लिए घर के बड़े , या फिर कार्यक्षेत्र में आस पास के लोग आपसे नाराज़ रह सकते हैं , बड़े अधिकारी लोगो की नाराजगी की वजह से नोकरी में परेशानी रहेगी । नोकरी और व्यवसाय में कोई बाधा ना आये इस के लिए उपाये के तौर पर धन भाव को मज़बूत करें , गुरुवार के दिन पीले चने की दाल मंदिर में अर्पित करें , और मस्तक पर ४३ दिनों तक हल्दी / केसर का तिलक करें , गुरु ग्रह का मन्त्र जाप करें । \uD83C\uDF39सिंह लग्न : गुरु ग्रह ५ वे और ८ वे भाव का स्वामी, लग्नेश सूर्य का मित्र होकर शुभकारी फल देने वाला ग्रह है । और अष्टमेश होने के कारण सुख दुख जीवन में अचानक आते हैं , और कभी कभी अचानक यात्रा का योग भी बन जाता है । गोचर ५ नवंबर से पंचम भाव में रहने से पंचम भाव से संबंधित विषयों से सुख मिलने के योग बनेंगे, जिनको प्रेमी / प्रेमिका या जीवनसाथी की तलाश है उनकी यह इच्छा पूरी होगी, नोकरी / व्यवसाय में तरक्की की इच्छा पूरी होगी । लग्न और भाग्य भाव पर दृष्टि होने से किसी अच्छी और प्रतिष्ठित स्थान पर नोकरी या शिक्षा प्राप्ति के योग बनेंगे । २३ जनवरी तक पंचमेश और सप्तमेश की युति के कारण विवाह होने के योग बनेंगे , अगर सप्तम भाव से संबंधित दशा चल रही है तो रिश्ता तय हो सकता है , या फिर अच्छी जगह नोकरी के योग बनेंगे । \uD83C\uDF39कन्या लग्न : गुरु ग्रह ४ था और ७ वा भाव का स्वामी , लग्नेश बुध का शत्रु ग्रह है इस लिए शुभकारी ग्रह नहीं । लेकिन क्योंकि गोचर ४ थे भाव में रहेगा शुभ भाव में होने से गुरु ग्रह शुभकारी परिणाम देगा । चतुर्थ भाव से संबंधित विषय ( घर, वाहन, मातृ सुख, मानसिक खुशी ) की प्राप्ति होगी , गुरु ग्रह की दृष्टि अष्टम और व्यय भाव पर होने से शारीरिक सुख की प्राप्ति, रोग से मुक्ति , धन और
